Jamison Brereton

66 (778)
Soma Pavama╠Дna, except Agni 19тАУ21
One hundred Vaikh─Бnasa poets
30 verses: g─Бyatr─л (except anuс╣гс╣нubh 18), arranged in trcas ╠е
This hymn sets larger rhetorical goals for itself than the last one and inhabits a less airless rhetorical space. Indeed, the hymn is in part about space: the con stricted area in which the soma is prepared and the materials employed in the preparation are likened to various cosmic domains and natural phenomena (see, e.g., vss. 2тАУ3, 5тАУ6, 12тАУ13). Soma himself is explicitly or implicitly identified with other deities and natural forces, and they with him: the sun (vss. 18, 22, 27), probably Indra (vs. 26), and especially Agni (vss. 19тАУ21). This last identification is so complete that the Anukramaс╣З─л identifies Agni as the divinity of this tr╠еcaтАФ not surprisingly, as it begins (vs. 19) with an address to Agni, who is assigned the archetypal Soma epithet тАЬself-purifyingтАЭ (vs. 20, with verbal forms in vss. 19 and 21), while also keeping his own characteristic vocabulary (esp. тАЬinstalled in frontтАЭ [puro╠Бhita] vs. 20).
The poet also seeks comradeship with Soma (vss. 1, 4, 14, 18), in addition to the usual good things.
From an Indo-European perspective, the hymn is notable for containing one of three R╠еgvedic occurrences of the famous phrase ├бkс╣гiti ┼Ыr├бvaс╕е тАЬimperishable fame,тАЭ cognate with Greek kle╠Бos a╠Бphthiton тАЬidem,тАЭ and the formula, identified by Adelbert Kuhn in 1853, that launched the field of comparative Indo-European poetics.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This is the second to the last of the composite G─Бyatr─л hymns in this maс╣Зс╕Нala; the last (IX.67) is attributed to a variety of named poets, while the Anukramaс╣З─л assigns this one to ┼Ыataс╣Г vaikh─Бnasaс╕е тАЬ100 Vaikh─Бnases.тАЭ Both attributions seems to acknowledge the composite nature of these compositions, as opposed to the previous ones, which have a single poet named for the whole hymn. Still, we would be hard-pressed to assemble 100 Vaikh─Бnases: only one, Vamra, is named in the Anukramaс╣З─л, as the author of X.99, a hymn to Indra, and the patronymic (and its underlying base) are both absent from the RVic text.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the place of these long hymns in the structure of the maс╣Зс╕Нala, see published introduction. to IX.61. All of these hymns consist of collections of tс╣Ыcas of varying degrees of cohesion. In fact, it is surprising how few tс╣Ыcas display a real attempt at thematic or lexical unity, and what they do show is often simply the byproduct of the fact that both the lexicon and thematic preoccupations of Maс╣Зс╕Нala IX are comparatively limited and so similar words and themes are not unlikely to show up in adjacent verses. This lack of unity contrasts, I think (this is my unsystematic and anecdotal impression) with collections of tс╣Ыcas in other maс╣Зс╕Нalas, notably VIII.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAll-seeing (Soma), who are the adorable friend (of the worshippers), flow for (us your) friends towards all (our) hymns of praise.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Purify yourself, you who are common to all the separate peoples,
(surging) toward all products of poetic skill,
a comrade for your comrades, to be reverently invoked.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The b p─Бda lacks a verb: Geldner supplies (silently) тАЬzu gewinnen,тАЭ Renou parenthetically тАЬpour (atteindre).тАЭ The p─Бda is found 3x elsewhere (IX.23.1, 62.25, 63.25); in two the vs. contains a form of тИЪsс╣Ыj тАШsurgeтАЩ (asс╣Ыgram 23.1, asс╣Ыkс╣гata 63.25) and I therefore supply that verb here.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The tс╣Ыca shows clear signs of unity, esp. lexically. Not only do all three vss.

contain a form of p├бva- (p├бvasva 1a, voc. pa/├бvam─Бna 2b, 3c), but the stem v├н┼Ыva- is found 4x (1a, b, 2a, 3b), kave (3c) echoes k─Б╠Бvya (1b), and pl. dh─Б╠Бm─Бni in 3a echoes du. dh─Б╠Бman─л in 2b. These тАЬdomainsтАЭ of vss 2-3 are thematically connected to the voc. vi┼Ыvacarс╣гaс╣Зe тАШcommon to all the separate peoplesтАЩ, in defining the spaces over which Soma holds sway.

FOR holy lore of every sort, flow onward thou whom all men love.
A Friend to be besought by friends.

L├дutere dich, bei allen V├╢lkern Bekannter, um alle Sehergaben zu gewinnen, als Freund f├╝r die Freunde anzurufen.

O riesle, aller Menschen Hort, uns alle Sehergaben her, Ein Freund den Freunden, preisenswerth.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, purified Soma, rule the universe by those two halves (of the lunar month) which stand facing you.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Those two halves: dh─Бman─л = p┼лrv─Бdipakс╣гau, the first and second fortnights of the lunar month, the sides or halves of the month resembling in their increase and decrease the sides of a creeper, whose leaves alternate; or, n─Бm─Бni aс╣Г┼Ыusom─Бtmake, the two names (aс╣Г┼Ыu and Soma); ‘on earth under the name aс╣Г┼Ыu by granting the desires of all mankind (Soma rules) this world; in heaven by giving the gods your lunar digits you are the winner of their affections. The gods drink the digits of the (moon) Soma by means of their growth and diminution one by one (i.e., as the moon waxes and wanes); dh─Бman─л probably means the two abodes (or stations) of the Soma

Jamison Brereton

From those two you rule over all, self-purifying oneтАФfrom the two domains [=Heaven and Earth]
that stand facing (each other), o Soma.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The issue in this vs. is the identify of the two dh─Б╠Бman─л; dependent on the answer to that is the function of the du. pronoun t─Б╠Бbhy─Бm, which could be instr., dat., or abl.

Answering the first question is made difficult by the fact that this is the only du. form of dh─Б╠Бman- in the RV. Geldner tr. тАЬFormenтАЭ (likewise Renou тАЬformesтАЭ) and in n. 2-3 explains these as the different stages (Stadien) the soma goes through in its preparation. This interpr. fails to explain the difference between the du. of vs. 2 and the pl. of 3; nor does it account for how Soma тАЬrules withтАЭ these forms (taking t─Б╠Бbhy─Бm as instr. as he does). RenouтАЩs interpr. of dh─Б╠Бman─л in 2 as the pure and mixed forms of soma provides a satisfactory account of the dual, but does not explain the transition to the pl. in 3 and again fails to explain how Soma rules with them. I take the term quite differently, as тАШdomainsтАЩ (rather than тАШformsтАЩ). In vs. 2 the dual refers to Heaven and Earth and alludes to the split of Soma into heavenly and earthly forms, a common trope in IX: he has a home in both places. Taking t─Б╠Бbhy─Бm as abl., I see Soma as ruling from both those polarized spaces, which together contain everything.

This interpr. gives prat─лc─л╠Бin c more content than the fairly empty renderings of Geldner (тАЬdie sich (uns) darbietenтАЭ) and Renou (тАЬqui se tiennent face (├а nous)тАЭ): Heaven and Earth as the two cosmic halves face each other.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The tс╣Ыca shows clear signs of unity, esp. lexically. Not only do all three vss.

contain a form of p├бva- (p├бvasva 1a, voc. pa/├бvam─Бna 2b, 3c), but the stem v├н┼Ыva- is found 4x (1a, b, 2a, 3b), kave (3c) echoes k─Б╠Бvya (1b), and pl. dh─Б╠Бm─Бni in 3a echoes du. dh─Б╠Бman─л in 2b. These тАЬdomainsтАЭ of vss 2-3 are thematically connected to the voc. vi┼Ыvacarс╣гaс╣Зe тАШcommon to all the separate peoplesтАЩ, in defining the spaces over which Soma holds sway.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSince your splendour abounds, you purified sage, Soma, are everywhere (associated) with the seasons.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

I.e. Soma whose attributes are the seasons such as spring, exists wherever day and night spread; because day and night are dependent on the Soma (i.e., the moon)

Jamison Brereton

The domains that are yours, Soma, you surround entirely
according to the ritual sequences, o self-purifying poet.1294 IX.66

Jamison Brereton Notes

My interpr. of the du. dh─Б╠Бman─л in 2 as the two cosmic domains allows the contrast between that form and the pl. dh─Б╠Бm─Бni to make sense. We have moved from the cosmic, to the ritual, in particular to the ritual ground - and here the pl. тАШdomainsтАЩ are the ritual spaces that Soma traverses and encloses. This change of venue and focus is signalled esp. by с╣Ыt├║bhiс╕е тАШaccording to the ritual sequencesтАЩ. Thus the themes of space and the cosmic reach of Soma that I identified as characteristic of this hymn find economical expression in the transition from the cosmic Soma in vs. 2 to the ritual Soma of vs. 3.

The main verb of this clause is p├бri тАж asi, in the formula vi┼Ыv├бtaс╕е p├бri тИЪas тАШsurround entirelyтАЩ (on which see my 1998 тАЬRigvedic vi┼Ыv├бtaс╕е s─лm, Or, Why Syntax Needs Poetics,тАЭ Fs. Watkins). Within this phrase we seem to have an embedded rel. cl. y─Б╠Бni te тАЬwhich are yours,тАЭ dependent on the obj. dh─Б╠Бm─Бni, and embedded relatives are generally blocked in the RV. But as we have noted elsewhere (see, e.g., comm. ad VI.21.2, 22.5), nominal rel. clauses are an exception to this rule, and here the y─Б╠Бni seems to be displaying (proto-)izafe behavior.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The tс╣Ыca shows clear signs of unity, esp. lexically. Not only do all three vss.

contain a form of p├бva- (p├бvasva 1a, voc. pa/├бvam─Бna 2b, 3c), but the stem v├н┼Ыva- is found 4x (1a, b, 2a, 3b), kave (3c) echoes k─Б╠Бvya (1b), and pl. dh─Б╠Бm─Бni in 3a echoes du. dh─Б╠Бman─л in 2b. These тАЬdomainsтАЭ of vss 2-3 are thematically connected to the voc. vi┼Ыvacarс╣гaс╣Зe тАШcommon to all the separate peoplesтАЩ, in defining the spaces over which Soma holds sway.

English translation:

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Pс╣Ыс╣гс╣нha = the lower part of heaven, i.e., the earth

Jamison Brereton

Yours are the gleaming rays that spread widely on the back of heaven across the filter, Soma, through your domains.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. seems to unite SomaтАЩs two theatres of operation, as laid out in vss. 2-3, the cosmic and the ritual. His тАЬgleaming raysтАЭ (reminiscent of the sun) spread both тАЬon the back of heavenтАЭ (div├бs pс╣Ыс╣гс╣нh├й) and across the ritual filter (pav├нtram); the instr. dh─Б╠Бmabhiс╕е тАЬthrough your domainsтАЭ can make reference both to this combining of cosmic and ritual and also, more specifically, to the limited ritual domains expressed by the pl. dh─Б╠Бm─Бni in vs. 3.

RenouтАЩs characterization in his n. - тАЬSoma-soleil тАж; en fait, lтАЩimage rituelle se combine avec lтАЩimage solaireтАЭ - expresses this rather nicely, though itтАЩs hard to get it from his tr. On the likening of the soma liquid on the filter to the sun, see IX.10.5 and comm. thereon.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe seven kindred (priests) uttering (praises) and worshipping (the gods with oblations) invoked you the sage at the sacrifice with hymns.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Seven kindred priests: Or, the seven kindred rivers urge you with thei rfingers, i.e., send you forth to be cleansed by the vasat─лvar─л and ekadhan─Б waters

Jamison Brereton

Together the seven siblings cried out to you, inciting with insightful thoughts
the inspired poet at the contest of Vivasvant.

Jamison Brereton Notes

It may not be clear in the published translation that тАЬyouтАЭ and тАЬthe inspired poetтАЭ are identical.

The referent of the тАЬseven siblingsтАЭ (sapt├б j─Бm├бyaс╕е) is disputed. Geldner identifies them as the fingers - and certainly j─Бm├н- is regularly used of the fingers of the officiants in IX.

But 1) do fingers тАЬcry outтАЭ? and more important, 2) why then тАЬsevenтАЭ? It seems unlikely that the poet would deliberately evoke an image of disfigurement or, at the very least, incompleteness. Ober (II.73; see II.71) tries to rescue this identification by suggesting that seven and ten are тАЬequivalentтАЭ indications of totality. But as he himself notes, a number of other groups of seven are mentioned in IX. A reference to one of these in this vs. would save us from positing an defective set of fingers. The most likely referent in my view are the seven streams, sapt├б s├нndhavaс╕е found two vss. earlier (6a). Rivers regularly make noise in the RV, and the proximity of that very phrase in vs. 6 tips the scales for me. Another feminine group of seven is the seven insightful thoughts, sapt├б dh─лt├бyaс╕е (IX.8.4, 9.4, 15.8, 62.17). dh─лt├н- also make noise, and they also (though not explicitly numbered 7) appear several vss. later doing just that: 11c ├бv─Бva┼Ыanta dh─лt├бyaс╕е тАЬthe insightful thoughts have bellowed.тАЭ However, supplying dh─лt├бyaс╕е here would lead to a poetically clumsy nearredundancy: the related dh─л╠Б-, also тАШinsightful thoughtтАЩ, is found in the same clause, and тАЬthe seven (inspired thoughts) cried out to you with inspired thoughtsтАЭ would be, to say the least, awk. (rather than being a pleasing etymological echo, at least to my mind). L├╝ders (246) also goes for streams, and Renou, citing his treatment, seems silently to endorse it. L├╝ders claims that Geldner identifies the seven as dh─лt├бyaс╕е, despite GeldnerтАЩs clear n. 1 тАЬDie Finger.тАЭ I donтАЩt see where L├╝ders got this - I assume itтАЩs simply a lapse.

In IX the figure Vivasvant seems to be the prototype sacrificer (see Oldenberg ad IX.99.2), perhaps in his role as father of Manu. For further on Vivasvant see published introduction. to I.139 as well as comm. to IX.99.2, X.14.5.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe fingers cleanse you in the quickly made loud-sounding (woollen) filter, when with a noise you are sprinkled with the water.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

In the quickly-made filter: Or, in the filter which overcomes guilt

Jamison Brereton

They groom you together, the unwed ones, on the sheepтАЩs *back, in the lively (water),
when, hoarse-voiced [/creaking], you are anointed [/greased] in the wood(en cup).

Jamison Brereton Notes

Since they are grooming (тИЪmс╣Ыj) him, the тАШunwed onesтАЩ (agr├║vaс╕е) are probably here the fingers, continuing the fem. pl. agent but modulating from streams to fingers (whose number is not specified here).

In b the phrase ├бdhi с╣гv├бс╣Зi is problematic. It is generally taken as a root noun loc. to тИЪsvan тАШsoundтАЩ: Grassmann, apparently Geldner (see his n. 9b and his locatival tr. тАЬunter GebrauseтАЭ), apparently Renou (but see his hesitations in his n.), Schindler (Rt. Noun p. 51, but see below), Ober (II.73)тАФthough Lubotsky lists it under a stem sv├бni-, so presumably interpr. it as a nom./acc. sg. neut. SchindlerтАЩs disc. suggests a slight variation on the root noun interpr., with the possibility that it is used here as an adj. тАШrauschendтАЩ modifying j─лr├бu, as Grassmann takes it.

In that case the independent sv├бn- was extracted from the compd tuvi-с╣гv├бс╣З- тАШpowerfully soundingтАЩ, an interpr. that seems over-elaborate.

Whether as root noun or an -i-stem, our form is equated with sv├бni in the similar p─Бda-final phrase ├бnu с╣гv├бс╣Зi in VI.46.14. However, I have demonstrated that sv├бni in that phrase must be a verb form, a 3rd sg. passive aor., as Oldenberg suggests. See comm. ad loc. Scarlatta, in a detailed disc. of the two sv├бni forms (676-77), suggests that our phrase, too, might contain a verb form. By his analysis p─Бda b is an (unsignalled) dependent cl., parallel to the y├бd clause of c, and so the accent on 3rd sg. sv├бni would be correct for a finite verb. He tr.

тАЬes putzen dich тАж, w├дhrend es ├╝ber der Wollseihe, unter dem fliessenden Wasser raschelt [und] w├дhrend du тАж gesalbt wirst.тАЭ This is clever, but I am disturbed by marking only one

  • and only the second - subordinate clause overtly. Moreover, this interpr. also must assume that there is a gapped subject to sv├бni or that it is used impersonally (both possibilities floated by Scarlatta). None of this is impossible, but the required assumptions and syntactic twists pile up.

I am drawn rather to an old suggestion of AufrechtтАЩs, endorsed by Oldenberg (but rejected explicitly by Schindler and Scarlatta) that ├бdhi с╣гv├бс╣Зi rests on ├бdhi *с╣гс╣З├бvi тАЬon (the sheepтАЩs) back.тАЭ Because of the morphological difficulties (the nonexistence of a loc. *sn├бvi to begin with), I would not posit AufrechtтАЩs intermediate form, but simply assume a reduction and metathetic scrambling of s─Б╠Бnavi, which occurs several times in the p─Бda-final phrase ├бdhi s─Б╠Бnavi (VI.48.5, IX.31.5, 37.4, 63.27); ├бdhi is the standard post- (/pre-)position in this expression; cf. also ├бdhi s─Б╠Бno avy├бye IX.86.3, 91.1, 96.13, 97.40 and numerous variants.

The presence of ├бvye at the beg. of the p─Бda would set the audienceтАЩs expectation for тАЬon the back of the sheep.тАЭ The presence of the тАЬnoiseтАЭ root тИЪsvar in the preceding vs. (8a asvaran) may have facilitated the metathesis, to produce a form appearing to belong to the phonologically and semantically similar root тИЪsvan, reinforced by rebh├б- in the flg. p─Бda.

In c I take rebh├бс╕е тАж ajy├бse as a pun, dependent on the literal sense of тИЪribh, which, rather than being тАШsingтАЩ as it generally is glossed, is really тАШcreak, raspтАЩ. See comm. ad VI.3.6. Here Soma is as usual тАШanointedтАЩ (ajyase) with milk, and in that regard he is identified as a rebh├б-, a ritual officiant with a particular voice quality. But as disc. ad VI.3.6, in a TS passage тИЪribh is used for a squeaky wheel, and of course the way to fix such a wheel is to тАЬgreaseтАЭ it (тИЪa├▒j). So the unmarked comparison here is тАЬ(as) a squeaky (wheel) is greased.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

This tс╣Ыca is thematically unified by the journey theme, reinforced by two forms of тИЪsс╣Ыj in vss. 10 (asс╣Ыkс╣гata) and 11 (├бsс╣Ыgram), the former in an etym. figure. Note the juxtaposition of the newer s-aor. 3rd pl. middle and the older root aorist, with no apparent functional or semantic difference. On these two formations see Narten (Sig.Aor. 270-71); she claims that they were originally differentiated functionally and still are occasionally (see IX.86.4), but in almost all occurrences this difference has been lost.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This tс╣Ыca is thematically unified by the journey theme, reinforced by two forms of тИЪsс╣Ыj in vss. 10 (asс╣Ыkс╣гata) and 11 (├бsс╣Ыgram), the former in an etym. figure. Note the juxtaposition of the newer s-aor. 3rd pl. middle and the older root aorist, with no apparent functional or semantic difference. On these two formations see Narten (Sig.Aor. 270-71); she claims that they were originally differentiated functionally and still are occasionally (see IX.86.4), but in almost all occurrences this difference has been lost.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndu, we abiding in your friendship, desiring to sacrifice, depending on your protection, desire your friendship.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Since we are likely to gain in comradeship with you, with you as our help,
we long for comradeship, o drop.

Jamison Brereton Notes

It is difficult to render the vs.-initial ├бsya te lit. тАЬof this here youтАЭ; the demon.

essentially exists as a prop for the enclitic te and a way to emphasize the 2nd ps. pronoun.

I do not know what the difference is between sakhy├б- and sakhitv├б-, or if any difference is meant. The former is far better attested and has a fuller paradigm, well distributed across cases and numbers (sg. and pl.); the latter is almost confined to the nom./acc. sg. (with 2 occurrences of the loc. sg.). In any case the vs. comes out a little flat: we want your comradeship because it will benefit us. The poet may have been trying to distract attention from this flatness by varying the derivational realization. ItтАЩs also worth noting that p─Бda a is also found in IX.61.29 without sakhitv├б- in context and p─Бda c is found in IX.31.6 without sakhy├б- in context.

In his endearingly crusty way, Bloomfield (Rig-Veda Repetitions ad IX.31.6) pronounces our vs. тАЬarrant nonsenseтАЭ: тАЬp─Бdas a and c, borrowed from good quarters, show that the stanza is irresponsible patchwork.тАЭ This seems rather harsh, but probably results in part from his interpr. of ├нyakс╣гantaс╕е as the desid. of тИЪyaj, rather than the now generally accepted derivation from тИЪ(n)a┼Ы; see comm. ad VI.21.3. Attributing it to тИЪyaj produces a participial phrase in b that has nothing to do with sakhy├й in a: тАЬIn thy friendship we, sacrificing with thy help, do we, O Indu, thy friendship craveтАЭ (BloomfieldтАЩs tr., which justifies his тАЬarrant nonsenseтАЭ judgment). Whereas a connection with тИЪ(n)a┼Ы sets out the reason we want your comradeshipтАФwe stand to gain from itтАФand makes ab a unified expression.

English translation:

тАЬFlow, Soma, for the mighty cattle-seeker, the beholder of men, enter Indra’s belly.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Purify yourself for the quest for cattle, for the great one of manly eye, o Soma.
Enter here into the belly of Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The usually idiomatic ─Б╠Бpavasva lacks the usual acc. object (тАЬbring [X] by purifying yourselfтАЭ). Perhaps the ─Б╠Бanticipates the ─Б╠Бin c, in the idiom ─Б╠БтАж vi┼Ыa тАШenterтАЩ.

The question in b are whether the two datives mah├й тАж nс╣Ыc├бkс╣гase belong together and what the referent(s) is/are. Geldner takes them together and identifies the referent as Indra, who appears by name in the next p─Бda, which would support GeldnerтАЩs solution. However, as Renou points out, nс╣Ыc├бkс╣гas- is never used of Indra, but generally of Agni or Soma. Renou himself separates the datives, supplying r├бс╣Зe with mah├й from the beginning of the tс╣Ыca (13a) and identifying the referent of nс╣Ыc├бkс╣гase as тАЬle dieu Soma.тАЭ Although the first choice seems possible and even reasonable, the second is awkward: it seems odd to order Soma to purify himself for himself, even if the addressee is the substance soma (which shouldnтАЩt actually have such agency) as distinct from the god. Given that the next tс╣Ыca but one (vss. 19-21) is addressed to Agni, that god seems a more likely choice. RenouтАЩs motivation in separating the two datives in b seems to be to wring the three functions out of the vs. (or, I gather, ab), but I donтАЩt see how they would match up. In any case, a modified tr. ├а la Renou, without reference to the three functions, is conceivable: тАЬтАж for the quest for cattle, for great (joy), for the one of manly eye [=Agni].тАЭ

English translation:

тАЬSoma, you are great, most worthy to be praised; Indu, (you are) the most vigorous of the mighty; engaged in battle you ever triumph.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Great are you, Soma, preeminent, strongest of the strong, o drop. Being a battler, you win every time.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As Renou points out, s├бn here is non-concessive. Instead it seems to have a function rather like the one I identified in III.30.5 (see comm. ad loc.), namely a definitional one: where, on the basis of the description of the godтАЩs activities or qualities, he is assigned an agentive title.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first two vss. are linked lexically and by their investment in grammatical comparison. The third is unconncected, but 18c echoes vs. 14 in the previous tс╣Ыca.

Griffith

Best art thou, Soma, of the great, Strongest of strong ones, Indu: thou
As Warrior ever hast prevailed.

Gro├Я bist du, Soma, der Oberste, o Saft, der Gewaltigen Gewaltigster. Als Streiter hast du jedesmal gesiegt.

Grassmann

Gross bist, Soma, du, der beste, Indu, und der starken st├дrkster, Stets bist Sieger du im Kampfe.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(You) who (are) mightier than the mighty, braver than the brave, more genitive rous than the genitive rous.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(You,) who are stronger even than the strong, more a champion even than champions,
more generous even than those who give much,

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. expands on the etymological figure and superlative phrase in 16b, ugr─Б╠Бс╣З─Бm тАж ├│jiс╣гс╣нhaс╕е, but with three pairs of comparatives, beginning with the ugr├йbhyaс╕е тАж ├│j─лy─Бn, lexically identical to the splv. phrase but morphologically different. The second is also an etym. figure, of less interest than the first because it lacks morphological variation: ┼Ы┼л╠Бrebhyaс╕е тАж ┼Ы┼л╠Бrataraс╕е. While the third substitutes a synonymic cmpd. for the abl. term: bh┼лrid─Б╠Бbhyaс╕е тАж m├бс╣Гh─лy─Бn тАЬmore generous than those who give much.тАЭ A low-key but pleasing set of variations on a phrasal theme.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first two vss. are linked lexically and by their investment in grammatical comparison. The third is unconncected, but 18c echoes vs. 14 in the previous tс╣Ыca.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, Soma, who are a hero (bestow) upon (us) food, (be) the giver of sons (to us); we choose you for your friendship, (we choose you) for your alliance.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, Soma, are the sun; (bring) refreshments here at the winning of the offspring of our own bodies.
We choose (you) for comradeship; we choose (you) for fellowship.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The sole Anuс╣гс╣нubh verse in a sea of G─Бyatr─лs. Note that it is the last vs. before the Agni tс╣Ыca, and so it may function as a closing or pseudo-closing vs., dividing the larger hymn into parts.

The first hemistich has received a variety of interpr., splitting into two major camps dependent in great part on the identity of s┼л╠Бraс╕е. Geldner (see his n. 18ab), Renou, Ober (I.494) take it as a gen. sg. of sv├аr-, one of a string of gen. dependent on s─Бt─Б╠БтАШat the winningтАЩ - hence, тАЬat the winning of the sun, refreshment, offspring, and bodies.тАЭ There are several arguments against this interp., however: 1) s┼л╠Бraс╕е has to be nom. sg. to s┼л╠Бra- in 22c, and so consistency would be nice (if not entirely necessary); 2) ├нс╣гaс╕е has the wrong accent for gen. sg. (expect iс╣г├бс╕е); 3) the standard interpr. of the sequence ├йс╣гaс╕е is ─Б╠Б├нс╣гaс╕е (already Pp., though see other poss. in GeldnerтАЩs n. 18ab), but the mid-p─Бda location of ─Б╠Б, between two supposedly parallel genitives, is an odd position for a preverb / adposition / adverb, and it has no obvious function in the clause. In fact the clause has no verb and no obvious one to supply - witness the variety of suggestions: Geldner тАЬ(stehst uns),тАЭ Renou тАЬ(qui tтАЩes pr├йpar├й),тАЭ Ober тАЬ(hilfst uns).тАЭ I therefore follow the path generally sketched by Oldenberg (see also L├╝ders 267 n. 4): a nominal equational cl. with nom. sg. s┼л╠Бraс╕е to s┼л╠Бra- (note that both Grassmann and Lubotsky so list the form), tv├бс╣Г soma s┼л╠Бraс╕е тАЬyou, Soma, are the sunтАЭ; followed by a 2nd cl. beginning with ─Б╠Б. Though ─Б╠Б remains mid-p─Бda, it is initial in its clause, as we would expect. An imperative of bringing / giving / suppying needs to be supplied, with acc. pl. ├нс╣гaс╕е (properly accented) as obj. Cf. expressions like III.53.1 … ├нс╣гa ─Б╠Бvahatam …, VI.52.16 … ├нс╣гa ─Б╠Бdhattam, and, with specifically Somian vocab., nearby IX.65.13 ─Б╠Б… ├нс╣гam p├бvasva тАЬBy purifying yourself, bring refreshment here.тАЭ More to the point, perhaps, the immediately following vs., 19b, ─Б╠Б suv├│rjam ├нс╣гaс╣Г ca naс╕е тАЬimpel hither nourishment and refreshment to us,тАЭ is quite similar and could provide the missing verb.

A structurally less crucial question is the relationship between the two genitives in b, tok├бsya тАж tan┼л╠Бn─Бm. As indicated above, Geldner takes them as parallel; Renou by contrast takes tan┼л╠Бn─Бm as a beneficial тАЬpour nous-m├кmes,тАЭ independent of the genitives dependent on s─Бt─Б╠Б. In the published translation I take them as nested, with tan┼л╠Бn─Бm dependent on tok├бsya, though I have no particular objection to the parallel interpr.

As noted above, vс╣Ыс╣З─лm├бhe sakhy─Б╠Бya is a permutation of 14c sakhitv├бm u┼Ыmasi.

On vс╣Ыс╣З─лm├бhe y├║jy─Бya, see comm. ad IX.88.1. Given the other exx. of this lexeme, I would now alter the tr. to тАЬwe choose you for yoking [/use].тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first two vss. are linked lexically and by their investment in grammatical comparison. The third is unconncected, but 18c echoes vs. 14 in the previous tс╣Ыca.

Griffith

Soma, as Sura, bring us food, win offspring of our bodies: we
Elect thee for our friendship, we elect thee for companionship.

Geldner

Du Soma stehst uns bei der Gewinnung der Sonne, der Speisegen├╝sse, der Nachkommenschaft und der eigenen Leiber bei. Wir erk├╝ren dich zur Freundschaft, wir erk├╝ren dich zur Bundesgenossenschaft.

Grassmann

Soma, du bist Sonne, schenkest Labung uns und unsern Kindern, Dich begehren wir zum B├╝ndniss.

English translation:

тАЬAgni, you support our lives, send us nutriment and food, drive far off the r─Бkс╣гasas.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O Agni, you bring (longer) lifespans through your purification; impel hither nourishment and refreshment to us.
Into the distance thrust misfortune.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Since pavase has an obj. ─Б╠Бy┼лс╣Гс╣гi, it would be desirable to have the preverb ─Б╠Б, which has transitivizing function with this root. This is easily done: ─Б╠Бy┼лс╣Гс╣гi can be decomposed into ─Б╠Б─Б╠Бy┼лс╣Гс╣гi without change to the Saс╣Гhit─Б text, though it is contra to the Pp.

This preverb in tmesis shows up apparently 2nd in the clause because it follows the zeroposition voc. ├бgne.

19-21 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

On this tс╣Ыca see published introduction. It is so insistently Agni-focused (all three vss.

begin with a form of that stem, two as voc.) that the Anukramaс╣З─л lists Agni as the deity of the three vss. But it is of course far more likely that Soma is being identified with Agni here.

The equation and poetic merging of these two ritual gods is found elsewhere, most notably in тАЬthe hardest hymn in the RVтАЭ (V.44), which is simultaneously applicable to both gods throughout its length. Their blending is shown here by the use of both Somian and Agnian vocab.: for the latter, see esp. pur├│hitaс╕е (20b); for the former, the three forms of p├бva-, one each in each vs.: 19a pavase, 20a p├бvam─Бnaс╕е, 21a pavasva. Note that after this Agni tс╣Ыca the word s├│ma- doesnтАЩt appear until vs. 29 and a likely identification with Indra (as well as comparison with the sun) intervenes.

Agni, thou pourest life; send down upon us food and vigorous strength;
Drive thou misfortune far away,

Keith

O Agni, thou purifiest life [7];
Do thou give food and strength to us;
Far away drive ill-fortune.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Jamison Brereton Notes

On this tс╣Ыca see published introduction. It is so insistently Agni-focused (all three vss.

begin with a form of that stem, two as voc.) that the Anukramaс╣З─л lists Agni as the deity of the three vss. But it is of course far more likely that Soma is being identified with Agni here.

The equation and poetic merging of these two ritual gods is found elsewhere, most notably in тАЬthe hardest hymn in the RVтАЭ (V.44), which is simultaneously applicable to both gods throughout its length. Their blending is shown here by the use of both Somian and Agnian vocab.: for the latter, see esp. pur├│hitaс╕е (20b); for the former, the three forms of p├бva-, one each in each vs.: 19a pavase, 20a p├бvam─Бnaс╕е, 21a pavasva. Note that after this Agni tс╣Ыca the word s├│ma- doesnтАЩt appear until vs. 29 and a likely identification with Indra (as well as comparison with the sun) intervenes.

English translation:

тАЬAgni, who are the doer of good, pour upon us brightness and fair-offspring; may he make me wealth and plural nty.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Agni, as a good worker, through your purification bring luster and an abundance of heroes for us,
establishing in me wealth and thriving.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Here, despite the obj. phrase in b, p├бvasva lacks the expected ─Б╠Б. It would technically be possible to take b with c: тАЬestablishing luster and an abundance of heroes for/in us, wealth and thriving in me,тАЭ which would leave pavasva intransitive. However, this seems artificial, and the existence of two 1st ps. pronouns in b and c, in different numbers, would be awkward. Moreover, 27c, with an independent d├бdhat clause, speaks in favor of separating b and c here.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On this tс╣Ыca see published introduction. It is so insistently Agni-focused (all three vss.

begin with a form of that stem, two as voc.) that the Anukramaс╣З─л lists Agni as the deity of the three vss. But it is of course far more likely that Soma is being identified with Agni here.

The equation and poetic merging of these two ritual gods is found elsewhere, most notably in тАЬthe hardest hymn in the RVтАЭ (V.44), which is simultaneously applicable to both gods throughout its length. Their blending is shown here by the use of both Somian and Agnian vocab.: for the latter, see esp. pur├│hitaс╕е (20b); for the former, the three forms of p├бva-, one each in each vs.: 19a pavase, 20a p├бvam─Бnaс╕е, 21a pavasva. Note that after this Agni tс╣Ыca the word s├│ma- doesnтАЩt appear until vs. 29 and a likely identification with Indra (as well as comparison with the sun) intervenes.

Jamison Brereton Notes

No strong signs of unity, though a form of p├бvam─Бna- opens vss. 22 and 24, but Soma as the sun in 22c returns in the theme of light and the defeat of darkness in 24bc.

The adj. vicakс╣гaс╣З├бс╕е тАШvisible afarтАЩ in 23c also participates in this imagery, partly matching vi┼Ыv├бdar┼Ыataс╕е тАШvisible to allтАЩ in the same position in 22c – though the Engl. tr. тАШvisibleтАЩ suggests a closer connection than exists in the Skt., which has тИЪdс╣Ы┼Ы in 22 but тИЪcakс╣г in 23.

The light imagery in this tс╣Ыca may pick up on the identification with Agni in the previous tс╣Ыca, while the verb j├бс╣Еghanat that closes the tс╣Ыca (24c) may modulate towards an identification with Indra, probably found in the following tс╣Ыca.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe purified (Soma) genitive rated the veracious all-pervading bright-shining light, destroying the black darkness.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The self-purifying one, as the lofty truth, has begotten the
gleaming light,
continually smashing (back) the black shades of darkness.

Jamison Brereton Notes

With L├╝ders (266), I take с╣Ыt├бс╣Г bс╣Ыh├бt as a nom. in apposition to Soma, rather than another acc. obj. to aj─лjanat as Geldner/Renou do. Either of course is possible; there are several passages in which an identification of Soma with с╣Ыt├б seems likely. See comm. ad IX.56.1.

But I would certainly accept an acc. interpr. as alternative.

22-24 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

No strong signs of unity, though a form of p├бvam─Бna- opens vss. 22 and 24, but Soma as the sun in 22c returns in the theme of light and the defeat of darkness in 24bc.

The adj. vicakс╣гaс╣З├бс╕е тАШvisible afarтАЩ in 23c also participates in this imagery, partly matching vi┼Ыv├бdar┼Ыataс╕е тАШvisible to allтАЩ in the same position in 22c – though the Engl. tr. тАШvisibleтАЩ suggests a closer connection than exists in the Skt., which has тИЪdс╣Ы┼Ы in 22 but тИЪcakс╣г in 23.

The light imagery in this tс╣Ыca may pick up on the identification with Agni in the previous tс╣Ыca, while the verb j├бс╣Еghanat that closes the tс╣Ыca (24c) may modulate towards an identification with Indra, probably found in the following tс╣Ыca.

Griffith

He, Pavamana, hath produced the lofty Law, the brilliant light,
Destroying darkness black of hue.

Geldner

Pavamana hat das hohe Gesetz, das helle Licht erschaffen, die schwarze Finsternis vertreibend.

Grassmann

Erhabnes Werk hat er erzeugt und helles Licht der flammende, Verjagend schwarze Finsterniss.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe gladsome swift-moving streams of the purified, green-tinted, unfadingly radiant (Soma), the destroyer (of darkness), have been let forth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Of the self-purifying one, continually smashing (back the darkness), of the tawny one, the glittering (drops) have surged,
lively ones with flickering radiance.

Jamison Brereton Notes

With Geldner and Renou, I supply тАШdarkness(es)тАЩ (t├бm─Бс╣Гsi) as obj. of j├бс╣Еghnataс╕е on the basis of 24c.

I supply тАШdropsтАЩ with candr─Б╠Бс╕е on the basis of III.40.4 candr─Б╠Бsa ├нndavaс╕е, though GeldnerтАЩs тАЬG├╝sseтАЭ and RenouтАЩs тАЬcoul├йes de somaтАЭ certainly fit the context, too. My тАЬdropsтАЭ is indirectly supported by the additional descriptor j─лr─Б╠Бс╕е тАШlivelyтАЩ, which is most commonly found in the cmpd. j─лr├б-d─Бnu- тАШhaving lively dropsтАЩ, with a different word for drop.

Note the play j─лr─Б╠Бajir├б-. The cmpd ajir├б-┼Ыocis- is a bit difficult to fit into context.

The 1st member ajir├б- means тАШquick, nimble, agileтАЩ, and the whole bahuvr─лhi occurs once elsewhere of Agni, VIII.19.13, where I tr. тАЬof nimble flame.тАЭ How this would apply to drops is not entirely clear; I assume it refers to the propensity of drops, esp. moving drops, to catch the light. It is also possible that ajir├б┼Ыociс╣гaс╕е is gen. sg. and modifies Soma, rather than nom. pl. modifying the drops. This would not appreciably change the image.

j├бс╣Еghnataс╕е in 25a, which picks up the same stem (in the nom. j├бс╣Еghanat) at the end of the immediately preceding p─Бda, 24c. As for internal unity, note the free phrase h├бre┼Ы candr─Б╠Бс╕е in 25b, which is transformed into the cmpd. h├бri┼Ыcandra-(only here in the RV, though prominent as a PN beginning in the Br.) in 26c. Superlatives also figure in the last two vss.: rath─л╠Бtama- 26a, ┼Ыubhr├б┼Ыastamaс╕е 26b, v─Бjas─Б╠Бtama- 27b.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe purified (Soma) possessing many chariots, most radiant with beauteous splendours, having green-tinted streams, attended by the Maruts.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The self-purifying one, the best charioteer, proclaimed as most
resplendent by the resplendent (Maruts),
gold-glittering, with the Maruts as his flock,

Jamison Brereton Notes

The Indraic cast of this vs. is quite clear, and I therefore think that Soma is being identified with Indra here (as he was with Agni in the tс╣Ыca 19-21). To begin with, the splv.

rath─л╠Бtama- is generally used of Indra (e.g., VIII.45.7); mar├║d-gaс╣Зa- тАШhaving the Maruts as his flockтАЩ is of course characteristic of Indra (e.g., VIII.89.2) and also expressed by other, similar but better-attested epithets like mar├║t-vant-. Moreover, the stem ┼Ыubhr├б- тАШresplendentтАЩ in the masc. pl., here in the instr. pl. ┼Ыubhr├йbhiс╕е, is almost always used of the Maruts (e.g., I.167.4).

The problem in the vs. is the splv. ┼Ыubhr├б┼Ыastamaс╕е in b. The interpr. reflected by Geldner and Renou stems from Oldenberg, who sees it as a haplology from *┼Ыubhr├б-┼Ыasta-tama-, i.e., the splv.

to a ppl. cmpd. Oldenberg himself doesnтАЩt provide a gloss, but on the basis of a cmpd. like kavi┼Ыast├б- тАШpraised by poetsтАЩ it should presumably be something like тАШmost praised by the resplendentтАЩ, though neither GeldnerтАЩs тАЬ├╝ber die anderen Sch├╢nen als der Sch├╢nste gepriesenтАЭ nor RenouтАЩs тАЬpar rapport aux (├кtres) beaux, il est le plus c├йl├йbr├й (quant ├а son fait dтАЩ├кtre) beauтАЭ reflects this presumption; that is, they do not take the 1st member as agent. Nor does the accent of the cmpd (either reconstructed or as attested) match that of kavi-┼Ыast├б-, though admittedly it does match the standard dev├б-hita- type. And the instr. ┼Ыubhr├йbhiс╕е seems an odd choice - we would expect a gen. pl. with the splv. of course; the anomalous instr. is surely responsible for the knots that Geldner and Renou tie themselves into, as well as GeldnerтАЩs cryptic (or disingenuous) n. 26b тАЬ┼Ыubhr├йbhiс╕е Instr. = Ablat. in Verbindung mit Superl. = Komparat.тАЭ The published translation represents a very different analysis, which I now think must be wrong: as the splv. to a root-noun cmpd. тАШproclaiming splendorтАЩ, but, as I realized all along, the accent is wrong (expect *┼Ыubhra-┼Ы├бs-(tama-)), and it is difficult to argue that the accent got misplaced because the word structure was misunderstood, esp. given the root noun cmpd splv. in the next vs., v─Бja-s─Б╠Б-tama- with correct accent. In addition, ┼Ыubhr├б- is an adj., тАШresplendentтАЩ, not a noun тАШsplendourтАЩ, and тИЪ┼Ыaс╣Гs doesnтАЩt take any form derived from тИЪ┼Ыubh as obj. So I now would reject the published translation and return to OldenbergтАЩs haplology - though with a semantic interpr. different from the Geldner/Renou complex. I would take the 1st member in agentive value, as is usual in such cmpds: тАЬmost praised by the resplendent (ones),тАЭ with the usual number neutralization. The reference is to the Maruts. What then of the independent instr. ┼Ыubhr├йbhiс╕е? Either it doubles the 1st cmpd member, whose function in the cmpd may have become unclear because of the haplology - hence тАЬmost praised by the resplendent (ones), by the resplendent ones.тАЭ Or it may be an instr. of accompaniment: тАЬmost praised by the resplendent (ones), along with the resplendent ones.тАЭ This would reflect the fact that the Maruts both praise Indra and receive praise themselves. This dual role of the Maruts, both praising and praised, is the subject of тАЬpoetic repairтАЭ in V.52, the first of ┼Ъy─Бv─Б┼ЫvaтАЩs Marut hymns. See comm. ad loc and reff. given there. Although I slightly favor the former explanation, English is better served by the latter, and I would now substitute the 2nd tr. just given; тАЬmost praisedтАЭ should also receive an asterisk.

Unfortunately тАЬgold-glitteringтАЭ for h├бri┼Ыcandra- obscures its relationship to h├бre┼Ы candr─Б╠Бс╕е in 25b тАЬof the tawny one, the glittering (drops).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

Each vs. opens with a form of p├бvam─Бna-, which also connects it with the preceding tс╣Ыca (see above). An even stronger link to the previous tс╣Ыca is the gen. intens. part.

j├бс╣Еghnataс╕е in 25a, which picks up the same stem (in the nom. j├бс╣Еghanat) at the end of the immediately preceding p─Бda, 24c. As for internal unity, note the free phrase h├бre┼Ы candr─Б╠Бс╕е in 25b, which is transformed into the cmpd. h├бri┼Ыcandra-(only here in the RV, though prominent as a PN beginning in the Br.) in 26c. Superlatives also figure in the last two vss.: rath─л╠Бtama- 26a, ┼Ыubhr├б┼Ыastamaс╕е 26b, v─Бjas─Б╠Бtama- 27b.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the purified Soma, the most liberal dispenser of food, pervade (the world) with his rays, granting excellent male offspring to the worshipper.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The self-purifying one will pervade with his rays, the best winner of prizes, establishing for the praiser an abundance of heroes.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In this vs. we seem to have returned to the identification of Soma with the sun, as shown esp. by ra┼Ыm├нbhiс╕е тАЬwith his raysтАЭ - this instr. pl. being reserved almost exclusively for the sunтАЩs rays (see, e.g., nearby IX.61.8 s┼л╠Бryasya ra┼Ыm├нbhiс╕е). The image is of the sun / Soma pervading space, with SomaтАЩs rays being the traces of the golden liquid as it spreads across the filter.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Each vs. opens with a form of p├бvam─Бna-, which also connects it with the preceding tс╣Ыca (see above). An even stronger link to the previous tс╣Ыca is the gen. intens. part.

j├бс╣Еghnataс╕е in 25a, which picks up the same stem (in the nom. j├бс╣Еghanat) at the end of the immediately preceding p─Бda, 24c. As for internal unity, note the free phrase h├бre┼Ы candr─Б╠Бс╕е in 25b, which is transformed into the cmpd. h├бri┼Ыcandra-(only here in the RV, though prominent as a PN beginning in the Br.) in 26c. Superlatives also figure in the last two vss.: rath─л╠Бtama- 26a, ┼Ыubhr├б┼Ыastamaс╕е 26b, v─Бjas─Б╠Бtama- 27b.

Griffith

May Pavamana, best to win the booty, penetrate with rays,
Giving the singer hero strength.

Geldner

Pavamana m├╢ge mit seinen Strahlen durchdringen, der am meisten Siegespreise gewinnt, der dem S├дnger die Meisterschaft verleiht.

Grassmann

Mit seinen Strahlen dringe durch der flammende, der Kraft verleiht, Dem S├дnger schenk’ er Heldenkraft.

English translation:

тАЬIndu when effused drops through the fleecy filter (into the vessel); being filtered Indu (enters) into Indra.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Being pressed, the drop has flowed forth across the fleecy filter;
being purified, the drop (has flowed) to Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. has two passively used participles, suv─Бn├бс╕е тАШbeing pressedтАЩ and pun─Бn├бс╕е тАШbeing purifiedтАЩ, which contrast with the agency implicitly accorded to Soma Pavam─Бna, тАЬself-purifyingтАЭ Soma. This more agentive participle returns in the final vs. (30b), just before we ask Soma for his favor.

The repetition of ├нnduс╕е (p─Бdas a and c) is somewhat clumsy, but the 2nd occurrences enables the usual word play with adjacent ├нndram.

Jamison Brereton Notes

No particular evidence of unity, except for an emphasis in the 1st two vss. on the technicalities of soma-preparation.

Griffith

Of thine which hath been brought from heaven.

(рдпрд╕реНрдп) рдЬрд┐рд╕ рдЖрдкрдХрд╛ (рджреНрдпреБрдореНрдирд╡рддреН) рджреАрдкреНрддрд┐рдпреБрдХреНрдд рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдп рдЬреЛ (рдкрдпрдГ)рджреНрдпреБрд▓реЛрдХ рд╕реЗ рджреБрд╣рд╛ рдЧрдпрд╛ рд╣реИ, (рджрд┐рд╡ рдЖрднреГрддрдореН) рдЙрд╕ рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдп рд╕реЗ (рддреЗрди) рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЗ (рдЬреАрд╡рд╕реЗ) рдЬреАрд╡рди рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдП (рдореГрд│) рд╕реБрдЦ рджреЗрдВреерейрежрее

рдЖрд░реНрдпрдореБрдирд┐ - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдХреЗ рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрд░реВрдкреА рдЕрдореГрдд рдХрд╛ рдЬрдм рддрдХ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдкрд╛рди рдирд╣реАрдВ рдХрд░рддрд╛, рддрдм рддрдХ рдЙрд╕рдХреЗ рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдп рдХреА рд╡реГрджреНрдзрд┐ рдХрджрд╛рдкрд┐ рдирд╣реАрдВ рд╣реЛрддреАред рдЗрд╕рд▓рд┐рдП рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рдЬреАрд╡рди рдХреА рд╡реГрджреНрдзрд┐ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдП рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╕рдВрдпрдо рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛ рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдЮрд╛ рдХрд╛ рдкрд╛рд▓рди рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖ резрежреж рд╡рд░реНрд╖ рдЬреАрдиреЗ рдХреА рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрд╛ рдХрд░реЗред рдЗрд╕ рдЕрднрд┐рдкреНрд░рд╛рдп рд╕реЗ рд╡реЗрджрдореЗрдВ рдЕрдиреНрдпрддреНрд░ рднреА рдХрд╣рд╛ рдЧрдпрд╛ рд╣реИ рдХрд┐ тАЬрдЬреАрд╡реЗрдо рд╢рд░рджрдГ рд╢рддрдореН, рдкрд╢реНрдпреЗрдо рд╢рд░рджрдГ рд╢рддрдореНтАЭ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ред рдЗрд╕реА рдЕрднрд┐рдкреНрд░рд╛рдп рд╕реЗ рдордиреБ-рдзрд░реНрдорд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рд╛ рд╣реИ рдХрд┐ тАЬрд╕рджрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реЗрдг рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рдГ рд╢рддрд╡рд░реНрд╖рд╛рдгрд┐ рдЬреАрд╡рддрд┐тАЭ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд░реНрдп рдЖрджрд┐ рд╡реНрд░рддреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рд╕реИрдХреЬреЛрдВ рдмрд░рд╕ рддрдХ рдЬреАрд╡рд┐рдд рд░рд╣рддрд╛ рд╣реИ реерейрежрее рдпрд╣ рдЫрд┐рдпрд╛рд╕рдард╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рдмрд╛рд░рд╣рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖрее

рдЖрд░реНрдпрдореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдкрд╡рдорд╛рди) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдкрд╛рд╡рдХ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдордиреН ! (рдпрд╕реНрдп) рдпрд╕реНрдп рднрд╡рддрдГ (рджреНрдпреБрдореНрдирд╡рддреН) рджреАрдкреНрддрд┐рдорддреН (рдкрдпрдГ) рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдВ (рджрд┐рд╡ рдЖрднреГрддрдореН) рджреНрдпреБрд▓реЛрдХрдЧрддреЛ рджреБрдЧреНрдзрдорд╕реНрддрд┐ (рддреЗрди) рддреЗрдиреИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреЗрдг (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ (рдЬреАрд╡рд╕реЗ) рдЬреАрд╡рдирдВ (рдореГрд│) рд╕реБрдЦрдп реерейрежрее рдЗрддрд┐ рд╖рдЯреНрд╖рд╖реНрдЯрд┐рддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее
